    22→/* ===== State ===== */
    23→let recognition     = null;
    24→let isListening     = false;
    25→let finalTranscript = '';
    26→let interimText     = '';
    27→let silenceTimer    = null;
    28→const SILENCE_DELAY = 3500; // ms of silence before auto-stop
    29→
    30→/* ===== Service Worker ===== */
    31→if ('serviceWorker' in navigator) {
    32→  navigator.serviceWorker.register('sw.js').catch(() => {/* silent */});
    33→}
    34→
    35→/* ===== Speech Recognition setup ===== */
    36→const SpeechRecognition = window.SpeechRecognition || window.webkitSpeechRecognition;
    37→
    38→if (!SpeechRecognition) {
    39→  notSupported.hidden = false;
    40→  micBtn.disabled = true;
    41→  micBtn.setAttribute('aria-disabled', 'true');
    42→} else {
    43→  initRecognition();
    44→}
    45→
    46→function initRecognition() {
    47→  recognition = new SpeechRecognition();
    48→  recognition.continuous     = true;
    49→  recognition.interimResults = true;
    50→  recognition.lang           = navigator.language || 'en-US';
    51→  recognition.maxAlternatives = 1;
    52→
    53→  recognition.onstart = () => {
    54→    isListening = true;
    55→    finalTranscript = '';
    56→    interimText = '';
    57→    setRecordingUI(true);
    58→  };
    59→
    60→  recognition.onresult = (event) => {
    61→    let interim = '';
    62→    for (let i = event.resultIndex; i < event.results.length; i++) {
    63→      const result = event.results[i];
    64→      if (result.isFinal) {
    65→        finalTranscript += result[0].transcript + ' ';
    66→      } else {
    67→        interim += result[0].transcript;
    68→      }
    69→    }
    70→    interimText = interim;
    71→    const displayText = (finalTranscript + interim).trim();
    72→    updateLiveText(displayText);
    73→
    74→    // Reset silence timer on every result
    75→    resetSilenceTimer();
    76→  };
    77→
    78→  recognition.onerror = (event) => {
    79→    // 'no-speech' is common and expected — just stop cleanly
    80→    if (event.error !== 'no-speech') {
    81→      console.warn('Speech recognition error:', event.error);
    82→    }
    83→    stopListening();
    84→  };
    85→
    86→  recognition.onend = () => {
    87→    // onend fires when recognition stops for any reason
    88→    if (isListening) {
    89→      // We didn't call stop manually yet; auto-stop happened
    90→      finishRecording();
    91→    }
    92→  };
    93→}
    94→
    95→function resetSilenceTimer() {
    96→  clearTimeout(silenceTimer);
    97→  silenceTimer = setTimeout(() => {
    98→    if (isListening) stopListening();
    99→  }, SILENCE_DELAY);
   100→}
   101→
   102→/* ===== Recording controls ===== */
   103→function startListening() {
   104→  if (!recognition || isListening) return;
   105→  hideTranscriptBar();
   106→
   107→  try {
   108→    recognition.start();
   109→  } catch (e) {
   110→    console.warn('Could not start recognition:', e);
   111→    // Re-init in case of invalid state
   112→    initRecognition();
   113→    try { recognition.start(); } catch (_) {}
   114→  }
   115→
   116→  resetSilenceTimer();
   117→}
   118→
   119→function stopListening() {
   120→  clearTimeout(silenceTimer);
   121→  isListening = false; // mark before calling stop so onend doesn't re-trigger finishRecording
   122→  if (recognition) {
   123→    try { recognition.stop(); } catch (_) {}
   124→  }
   125→  finishRecording();
   126→}
   127→
   128→function finishRecording() {
   129→  setRecordingUI(false);
   130→  const text = finalTranscript.trim();
   131→  if (text) {
   132→    showTranscriptBar(text);
   133→  }
   134→}
   135→
   136→/* ===== UI state helpers ===== */
   137→function setRecordingUI(recording) {
   138→  micBtn.classList.toggle('recording', recording);
   139→  micRing.classList.toggle('recording', recording);
   140→  micBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', recording ? 'true' : 'false');
   141→  micBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', recording ? 'Stop recording' : 'Start recording');
   142→  micHint.textContent = recording ? 'Tap to stop' : 'Tap to speak';
   143→  micHint.classList.toggle('active', recording);
   144→  liveTranscript.hidden = !recording;
   145→  if (!recording) {
   146→    liveText.textContent = 'Listening…';
   147→    liveText.classList.remove('has-text');
   148→  }
   149→}
   150→
   151→function updateLiveText(text) {
   152→  if (text) {
   153→    liveText.textContent = text;
   154→    liveText.classList.add('has-text');
   155→  } else {
   156→    liveText.textContent = 'Listening…';
   157→    liveText.classList.remove('has-text');
   158→  }
   159→}
   160→
   161→function showTranscriptBar(text) {
   162→  transcriptText.textContent = text;
   163→  transcriptBar.hidden = false;
   164→}
   165→
   166→function hideTranscriptBar() {
   167→  transcriptBar.hidden = true;
   168→  transcriptText.textContent = '';
   169→}
   170→
   171→/* ===== Mic button click (toggle) ===== */
   172→micBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {
   173→  if (isListening) {
   174→    stopListening();
   175→  } else {
   176→    startListening();
   177→  }
   178→});
   179→
   180→/* ===== Send / Discard ===== */
   181→sendBtn.addEventListener('click', async () => {
   182→  const text = transcriptText.textContent.trim();
   183→  if (!text) return;
   184→  hideTranscriptBar();
   185→  await sendMessage(text);
   186→});
   187→
   188→discardBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {
   189→  hideTranscriptBar();
   190→});
   191→
   192→/* ===== Webhook send ===== */
   193→async function sendMessage(text) {
   194→  const webhookUrl = localStorage.getItem('webhookUrl') || '';
   195→  const timestamp  = new Date().toISOString();
   196→  const payload    = { text, source: 'hey-chill', timestamp };
   197→
   198→  // Add message to history immediately
   199→  const msgEl = addMessage(text, timestamp, 'sending');
   200→
   201→  if (!webhookUrl) {
   202→    updateMessageStatus(msgEl, 'no-webhook');
   203→    return;
   204→  }
   205→
   206→  try {
   207→    const res = await fetch(webhookUrl, {
   208→      method: 'POST',
   209→      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
   210→      body: JSON.stringify(payload),
   211→    });
   212→    if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}`);
   213→    updateMessageStatus(msgEl, 'sent');
   214→  } catch (err) {
   215→    console.warn('Webhook error:', err);
   216→    updateMessageStatus(msgEl, 'error');
   217→  }
   218→}
   219→
   220→/* ===== Message history ===== */
   221→function addMessage(text, timestamp, status) {
   222→  // Hide empty state
   223→  messagesEmpty.style.display = 'none';
   224→
   225→  const el = document.createElement('div');
   226→  el.className = `message ${status}`;
   227→
   228→  const timeStr = new Date(timestamp).toLocaleTimeString([], {
   229→    hour: '2-digit',
   230→    minute: '2-digit',
   231→  });
   232→
   233→  const statusLabel = {
   234→    sending:    'Sending…',
   235→    sent:       'Sent',
   236→    error:      'Failed',
   237→    'no-webhook': 'No webhook',
   238→  };
   239→
   240→  el.innerHTML = `
   241→    <p class="message-text">${escapeHtml(text)}</p>
   242→    <div class="message-meta">
   243→      <span class="message-time">${timeStr}</span>
   244→      <span class="message-status">${statusLabel[status] || status}</span>
   245→    </div>
   246→  `;
   247→
   248→  messagesEl.appendChild(el);
   249→  el.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth', block: 'end' });
   250→  return el;
   251→}
   252→
   253→function updateMessageStatus(el, status) {
   254→  el.className = `message ${status}`;
   255→  const statusEl = el.querySelector('.message-status');
   256→  const labels = {
   257→    sent:         'Sent',
   258→    error:        'Failed',
   259→    'no-webhook': 'No webhook set',
   260→  };
   261→  if (statusEl) statusEl.textContent = labels[status] || status;
   262→}
   263→
   264→function escapeHtml(str) {
   265→  return str
   266→    .replace(/&/g, '&amp;')
   267→    .replace(/</g, '&lt;')
   268→    .replace(/>/g, '&gt;')
   269→    .replace(/"/g, '&quot;')
   270→    .replace(/'/g, '&#39;');
   271→}
   272→
   273→/* ===== Settings modal ===== */
   274→settingsBtn.addEventListener('click', openSettings);
   275→modalClose.addEventListener('click',  closeSettings);
   276→modalOverlay.addEventListener('click', (e) => {
   277→  if (e.target === modalOverlay) closeSettings();
   278→});
   279→
   280→document.addEventListener('keydown', (e) => {
   281→  if (e.key === 'Escape') closeSettings();
   282→});
   283→
   284→saveSettings.addEventListener('click', () => {
   285→  const url = webhookInput.value.trim();
   286→  localStorage.setItem('webhookUrl', url);
   287→  closeSettings();
   288→});
   289→
   290→function openSettings() {
   291→  webhookInput.value = localStorage.getItem('webhookUrl') || '';
   292→  modalOverlay.hidden = false;
   293→  webhookInput.focus();
   294→}
   295→
   296→function closeSettings() {
   297→  modalOverlay.hidden = true;
   298→}

Now I understand the existing codebase. Let me also read the style.css and other files to understand the full picture. The issue requires implementing wake word detection for "Hey Chill". The app is a PWA that uses Web Speech API for recording. I need to add passive listening for "Hey Chill" keyword that triggers recording. Let me understand the acceptance criteria: 1. Say "Hey Chill" and the app starts recording 2. False positive rate is low enough to be usable 3. Works in Chrome on desktop and mobile Approach: Since this is a POC with 80% reliability acceptable, I'll use the Web Speech API with continuous recognition. I'll need to run a separate continuous wake word listener that monitors for "hey chill" and switches to the main recording flow when detected. Since Chrome can't run multiple SpeechRecognition instances at once, I'll manage the state transitions carefully—stopping the wake word listener and starting the main recording when the keyword is found. I'll also add a UI toggle to enable/disable wake word detection and show a visual indicator when it's actively listening. interimResults: true to catch phrases as they're being spoken - When "hey chill" is detected, strip the wake word from the transcript before showing it to the user - Need to auto-restart the wake word listener after each recognition session ends (Chrome sometimes stops it) - Mobile Chrome requires user gesture to start microphone, so wake word mode needs to be explicitly enabled For the implementation, I'll create a separate wake word detector instance and add a toggle in the UI. The flow alternates between wake word listening and recording mode: start wake word detection, stop it when "hey chill" is recognized, begin the actual recording, then restart wake word listening once done. I'll add a visual indicator for when wake word mode is active and handle false positives by matching the full phrase case-insensitively with fuzzy matching for common mishearings like "hey jill" or "a chill". For a proof-of-concept, a simple substring match should be sufficient. Now I need to check the existing CSS patterns to see what styling conventions are already in place.

ASSISTANTMESSAGE #18
Now I have a full understanding of the codebase. Let me plan the implementation: ## Wake Word Detection Approach Since the issue says "Web Speech API continuous listening, lightweight JS library, or other browser-compatible approach" and the target is Chrome, I'll use the Web Speech API continuous listening approach. This is a POC, so 80% reliability is acceptable. ### Implementation Plan 1. **Wake word mode**: A separate, continuously-running SpeechRecognition instance that listens for "hey chill" 2. **Flow**: - Wake mode ON: `wakeRecognition` listens continuously with `interimResults: true` - When "hey chill" detected in transcript: stop wake recognition → start main recording - After main recording ends: restart wake recognition 3. **UI Changes**: - Add a "wake word" toggle button in the header - Show a visual indicator when wake word is active (e.g., pulsing badge or different state) - Update mic hint to say "Say 'Hey Chill' to start" when wake mode is active ### Key Implementation Details For pattern matching, I'll handle "hey chill" case-insensitively with some fuzzy matching to catch variations like "hey chil" or similar mishearings. There's a Chrome quirk where SpeechRecognition stops after 5-60 seconds of silence, so I need to auto-restart the wake recognition session when it ends unless the user disabled wake mode or we're actively recording. The state machine tracks whether wake mode is enabled, ensures wake recognition only runs when not in main recording mode, and automatically restarts it once the main recording finishes. Since Chrome can't handle two simultaneous SpeechRecognition instances, I need to make sure only one runs at a time. For the UI, I'm adding a wake word toggle button in the header and a status indicator to show when wake mode is active, along with some styling to reflect the active state. Setting up the JavaScript to handle wake word detection... Setting up the speech recognition event handlers... Now I'm defining a helper to check if the transcript matches any wake phrases, then implementing the start and stop functions for the recognition service with error handling for invalid states, and scheduling automatic restarts when the recognition ends unexpectedly. Setting up the wake word detection handler that pauses recognition briefly before starting the main listening mode, and the enable function that activates wake mode, updates the UI, persists the preference, and kicks off recognition if we're not already listening. Now I'm adding the disable function to turn off wake mode, clearing the active state and stopping recognition, then creating a hint updater that shows contextual text based on whether wake mode is active, and finally wiring up the button click handler to toggle between these two states. I need to restore the wake mode preference from localStorage on page load, then handle the interaction between wake recognition and the main speech recognition since Chrome won't let both run simultaneously—when the user starts listening, I need to make sure the wake recognition stops first, and once they finish recording, I should restart it if wake mode is still enabled. Updating the listening functions... Now I'm realizing the hint text needs to reflect wake mode state—when wake mode is active and recording finishes, it should prompt the user to say the wake word or tap, not just "Tap to speak". I need to either update `setRecordingUI` to accept a wake mode parameter or adjust the hint after calling it. Option 2 is simpler—I'll just call `updateWakeHint()` right after `setRecordingUI(false)` in `finishRecording` to override the generic hint with the wake-mode-specific one. Next I need to add the wake word button to the HTML interface. Writing SVG icon... Writing the antenna icon... Still writing styles... Now I'm reconsidering the header structure—I should place the wake button alongside the settings button in a dedicated actions container rather than having it standalone, so both controls sit together on the right side of the header. I'm also thinking through how the wake word detection works: when the wake recognition picks up "hey chill", it triggers the main recording to start, but I need to figure out whether the main transcript will include that wake phrase or if it gets stripped automatically by the speech recognition API. with the hint text. Looking at the timing, "Hey Chill" takes about half a second to speak, and with the wake recognition stopping plus the 300ms delay before main recording starts, there's roughly a 0.5-0.8 second window—so if the user pauses briefly after the wake word, the transition should work smoothly. I also need to handle the edge case where main recording fails to start after detecting the wake word, which means re-enabling wake mode, and I should think through what happens when the user stops recording mid-session. Now I'm working through the complete implementation, keeping in mind that the issue requires this to work while the PWA is in the foreground. For the wake word itself, I want to keep false positives low, so I'll stick with "hey chill" as the primary match and maybe include one variant, but I need to be careful not to cast the net too wide. Let me outline the changes needed: I'll add a wake word toggle button in the header alongside the settings button, include a visual indicator showing when wake mode is active, and update the HTML and CSS to support these new elements. For the JavaScript, I need to set up wake word recognition with helper functions to initialize, start, and stop the detection, handle when the phrase is detected, and manage the UI state accordingly. I'll also need to integrate this with the existing listening flow so wake recognition pauses when the user starts speaking, then resumes afterward. Writing the HTML structure... Still writing the implementation... Still writing the transition logic... Now I'm ready to create the git branch and implement these changes.

'Say \"Hey Chill\" or tap' : 'Tap to speak';\n  }\n}\n\nwakeBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {\n  if (wakeMode) {\n    disableWakeMode();\n  } else {\n    enableWakeMode();\n  }\n});\n\n// Restore wake mode preference across sessions\nif (SpeechRecognition && localStorage.getItem('wakeMode') === '1') {\n  enableWakeMode();\n}"

   103→function resetSilenceTimer() {
   104→  clearTimeout(silenceTimer);
   105→  silenceTimer = setTimeout(() => {
   106→    if (isListening) stopListening();
   107→  }, SILENCE_DELAY);
   108→}
   109→
   110→/* ===== Recording controls ===== */
   111→function startListening() {
   112→  if (!recognition || isListening) return;
   113→  hideTranscriptBar();
   114→
   115→  // Ensure wake recognition is stopped before starting main recording
   116→  if (wakeMode) stopWakeRecognition();
   117→
   118→  try {
   119→    recognition.start();
   120→  } catch (e) {
   121→    console.warn('Could not start recognition:', e);
   122→    // Re-init in case of invalid state
   123→    initRecognition();
   124→    try { recognition.start(); } catch (_) {}
   125→  }
   126→
   127→  resetSilenceTimer();
   128→}
   129→
   130→function stopListening() {
   131→  clearTimeout(silenceTimer);
   132→  isListening = false; // mark before calling stop so onend doesn't re-trigger finishRecording
   133→  if (recognition) {
   134→    try { recognition.stop(); } catch (_) {}
   135→  }
   136→  finishRecording();
   137→}
   138→
   139→function finishRecording() {
   140→  setRecordingUI(false);
   141→  const text = finalTranscript.trim();
   142→  if (text) {
   143→    showTranscriptBar(text);
   144→  }
   145→  // Resume passive wake word listening if mode is active
   146→  if (wakeMode) scheduleWakeRestart();
   147→  updateWakeHint();
   148→}
   149→
   150→/* ===== UI state helpers ===== */
   151→function setRecordingUI(recording) {
   152→  micBtn.classList.toggle('recording', recording);
   153→  micRing.classList.toggle('recording', recording);
   154→  micBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', recording ? 'true' : 'false');
   155→  micBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', recording ? 'Stop recording' : 'Start recording');
   156→  micHint.textContent = recording ? 'Tap to stop' : (wakeMode ? 'Say "Hey Chill" or tap' : 'Tap to speak');
   157→  micHint.classList.toggle('active', recording);
   158→  liveTranscript.hidden = !recording;
   159→  if (!recording) {
   160→    liveText.textContent = 'Listening…';
   161→    liveText.classList.remove('has-text');
   162→  }
   163→}
   164→
   165→function updateLiveText(text) {
   166→  if (text) {
   167→    liveText.textContent = text;
   168→    liveText.classList.add('has-text');
   169→  } else {
   170→    liveText.textContent = 'Listening…';
   171→    liveText.classList.remove('has-text');
   172→  }
   173→}
   174→
   175→function showTranscriptBar(text) {
   176→  transcriptText.textContent = text;
   177→  transcriptBar.hidden = false;
   178→}
   179→
   180→function hideTranscriptBar() {
   181→  transcriptBar.hidden = true;
   182→  transcriptText.textContent = '';
   183→}
   184→
   185→/* ===== Mic button click (toggle) ===== */
   186→micBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {
   187→  if (isListening) {
   188→    stopListening();
   189→  } else {
   190→    startListening();
   191→  }
   192→});
   193→
   194→/* ===== Send / Discard ===== */

   198→  hideTranscriptBar();

   303→
   304→function openSettings() {
   305→  webhookInput.value = localStorage.getItem('webhookUrl') || '';
   306→  modalOverlay.hidden = false;
   307→  webhookInput.focus();
   308→}
   309→
   310→function closeSettings() {
   311→  modalOverlay.hidden = true;
   312→}
   313→
   314→/* ===== Wake Word Detection ===== */
   315→
   316→function isWakePhrase(transcript) {
   317→  return WAKE_PHRASES.some(phrase => transcript.includes(phrase));
   318→}
   319→
   320→function initWakeRecognition() {
   321→  wakeRecognition = new SpeechRecognition();
   322→  wakeRecognition.continuous     = true;
   323→  wakeRecognition.interimResults = true;
   324→  wakeRecognition.lang           = navigator.language || 'en-US';
   325→  wakeRecognition.maxAlternatives = 1;
   326→
   327→  wakeRecognition.onresult = (event) => {
   328→    for (let i = event.resultIndex; i < event.results.length; i++) {
   329→      const transcript = event.results[i][0].transcript.toLowerCase().trim();
   330→      if (isWakePhrase(transcript)) {
   331→        handleWakeWordDetected();
   332→        return;
   333→      }
   334→    }
   335→  };
   336→
   337→  wakeRecognition.onerror = (event) => {
   338→    if (event.error === 'not-allowed' || event.error === 'service-not-allowed') {
   339→      // Microphone access denied — silently disable wake mode
   340→      disableWakeMode();
   341→      return;
   342→    }
   343→    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
   344→      scheduleWakeRestart();
   345→    }
   346→  };
   347→
   348→  wakeRecognition.onend = () => {
   349→    // Chrome stops continuous recognition periodically — restart unless we
   350→    // deliberately stopped it to hand off to main recording.
   351→    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
   352→      scheduleWakeRestart();
   353→    }
   354→  };
   355→}
   356→
   357→function startWakeRecognition() {
   358→  if (!wakeRecognition) initWakeRecognition();
   359→  wakeTriggered = false;
   360→  try {
   361→    wakeRecognition.start();
   362→  } catch (e) {
   363→    // InvalidStateError when already started — reinit and retry
   364→    initWakeRecognition();
   365→    try { wakeRecognition.start(); } catch (_) {}
   366→  }
   367→}
   368→
   369→function stopWakeRecognition() {
   370→  if (wakeRecognition) {
   371→    try { wakeRecognition.stop(); } catch (_) {}
   372→  }
   373→}
   374→
   375→function scheduleWakeRestart() {
   376→  clearTimeout(wakeRestartTimer);
   377→  wakeRestartTimer = setTimeout(() => {
   378→    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
   379→      startWakeRecognition();
   380→    }
   381→  }, 300);
   382→}
   383→
   384→function handleWakeWordDetected() {
   385→  if (isListening || wakeTriggered) return;
   386→  wakeTriggered = true;
   387→  stopWakeRecognition();
   388→  // Give the recognition engine a moment to fully stop before starting main recording
   389→  setTimeout(() => {
   390→    wakeTriggered = false;
   391→    startListening();
   392→  }, 250);
   393→}
   394→
   395→function enableWakeMode() {
   396→  wakeMode = true;
   397→  wakeBtn.classList.add('wake-active');
   398→  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', 'true');
   399→  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', 'Disable wake word');
   400→  wakeBtn.title = 'Wake word: ON';
   401→  localStorage.setItem('wakeMode', '1');
   402→  updateWakeHint();
   403→  if (!isListening) startWakeRecognition();
   404→}
   405→
   406→function disableWakeMode() {
   407→  wakeMode = false;
   408→  wakeBtn.classList.remove('wake-active');
   409→  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', 'false');
   410→  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', 'Enable wake word');
   411→  wakeBtn.title = 'Wake word: Hey Chill';
   412→  localStorage.setItem('wakeMode', '0');
   413→  clearTimeout(wakeRestartTimer);
   414→  stopWakeRecognition();
   415→  updateWakeHint();
   416→}
   417→
   418→function updateWakeHint() {
   419→  if (!isListening) {
   420→    micHint.textContent = wakeMode ? 'Say "Hey Chill" or tap' : 'Tap to speak';
   421→  }
   422→}
   423→
   424→wakeBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {
   425→  if (wakeMode) {
   426→    disableWakeMode();
   427→  } else {
   428→    enableWakeMode();
   429→  }

 function closeSettings() {
   modalOverlay.hidden = true;
 }
+
+/* ===== Wake Word Detection ===== */
+
+function isWakePhrase(transcript) {
+  return WAKE_PHRASES.some(phrase => transcript.includes(phrase));
+}
+
+function initWakeRecognition() {
+  wakeRecognition = new SpeechRecognition();
+  wakeRecognition.continuous     = true;
+  wakeRecognition.interimResults = true;
+  wakeRecognition.lang           = navigator.language || 'en-US';
+  wakeRecognition.maxAlternatives = 1;
+
+  wakeRecognition.onresult = (event) => {
+    for (let i = event.resultIndex; i < event.results.length; i++) {
+      const transcript = event.results[i][0].transcript.toLowerCase().trim();
+      if (isWakePhrase(transcript)) {
+        handleWakeWordDetected();
+        return;
+      }
+    }
+  };
+
+  wakeRecognition.onerror = (event) => {
+    if (event.error === 'not-allowed' || event.error === 'service-not-allowed') {
+      // Microphone access denied — silently disable wake mode
+      disableWakeMode();
+      return;
+    }
+    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
+      scheduleWakeRestart();
+    }
+  };
+
+  wakeRecognition.onend = () => {
+    // Chrome stops continuous recognition periodically — restart unless we
+    // deliberately stopped it to hand off to main recording.
+    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
+      scheduleWakeRestart();
+    }
+  };
+}
+
+function startWakeRecognition() {
+  if (!wakeRecognition) initWakeRecognition();
+  wakeTriggered = false;
+  try {
+    wakeRecognition.start();
+  } catch (e) {
+    // InvalidStateError when already started — reinit and retry
+    initWakeRecognition();
+    try { wakeRecognition.start(); } catch (_) {}
+  }
+}
+
+function stopWakeRecognition() {
+  if (wakeRecognition) {
+    try { wakeRecognition.stop(); } catch (_) {}
+  }
+}
+
+function scheduleWakeRestart() {
+  clearTimeout(wakeRestartTimer);
+  wakeRestartTimer = setTimeout(() => {
+    if (wakeMode && !isListening && !wakeTriggered) {
+      startWakeRecognition();
+    }
+  }, 300);
+}
+
+function handleWakeWordDetected() {
+  if (isListening || wakeTriggered) return;
+  wakeTriggered = true;
+  stopWakeRecognition();
+  // Give the recognition engine a moment to fully stop before starting main recording
+  setTimeout(() => {
+    wakeTriggered = false;
+    startListening();
+  }, 250);
+}
+
+function enableWakeMode() {
+  wakeMode = true;
+  wakeBtn.classList.add('wake-active');
+  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', 'true');
+  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', 'Disable wake word');
+  wakeBtn.title = 'Wake word: ON';
+  localStorage.setItem('wakeMode', '1');
+  updateWakeHint();
+  if (!isListening) startWakeRecognition();
+}
+
+function disableWakeMode() {
+  wakeMode = false;
+  wakeBtn.classList.remove('wake-active');
+  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-pressed', 'false');
+  wakeBtn.setAttribute('aria-label', 'Enable wake word');
+  wakeBtn.title = 'Wake word: Hey Chill';
+  localStorage.setItem('wakeMode', '0');
+  clearTimeout(wakeRestartTimer);
+  stopWakeRecognition();
+  updateWakeHint();
+}
+
+function updateWakeHint() {
+  if (!isListening) {
+    micHint.textContent = wakeMode ? 'Say "Hey Chill" or tap' : 'Tap to speak';
+  }
+}
+
+wakeBtn.addEventListener('click', () => {
+  if (wakeMode) {
+    disableWakeMode();
+  } else {
+    enableWakeMode();
+  }
+});
+
+// Restore wake mode preference across sessions
+if (SpeechRecognition && localStorage.getItem('wakeMode') === '1') {
+  enableWakeMode();
+}

--- ## Status DONE ## What Changed - `index.html` — added `header-actions` flex wrapper; added wake word toggle button with broadcast-waves SVG icon before the settings button - `style.css` — added `.header-actions` flex container; added `.icon-btn.wake-active` with accent-colour pulsing animation - `app.js` — added `wakeBtn` DOM ref; added wake state variables (`wakeRecognition`, `wakeMode`, `wakeTriggered`, `wakeRestartTimer`, `WAKE_PHRASES`); added full wake word detection subsystem (init/start/stop/restart/enable/disable/update-hint); modified `startListening` to stop wake recognition before main recording starts; modified `finishRecording` to restart wake recognition after recording ends; updated `setRecordingUI` hint text to reflect wake mode ## Key Decisions - **Two SpeechRecognition instances** (one for wake word, one for main recording) rather than a third-party library — keeps zero dependencies and works in Chrome with the Web Speech API the app already uses - **250 ms handoff pause** between stopping wake recognition and starting main recording — Chrome throws `InvalidStateError` if you call `.start()` immediately after `.stop()` - **`wakeTriggered` flag** prevents the `onend` auto-restart loop from firing during the intentional stop → start transition - **`scheduleWakeRestart` (300 ms timer)** handles Chrome's periodic automatic stopping of continuous recognition sessions ## PR / Branch - Branch: `feature/frg-252-wake-word-detection` - PR: https://github.com/chillkimtest-oss/hey-chill/pull/2
